\n\n\t\n\t\n\t

apply_filters( string $tag, mixed $value )

\n\n\t
\n\t\t

Call the functions added to a filter hook.

\n\t
\n\n\n\t\n\t

Contents

\n
\n\n
\n
\n\t

Description #Description

\n\t

The callback functions attached to filter hook $tag are invoked by calling this function. This function can be used to create a new filter hook by simply calling this function with the name of the new hook specified using the $tag parameter.

\n

The function allows for additional arguments to be added and passed to hooks.

\n
// Our filter callback function\nfunction example_callback( $string, $arg1, $arg2 ) {\n    // (maybe) modify $string\n    return $string;\n}\nadd_filter( 'example_filter', 'example_callback', 10, 3 );\n\n/*\n * Apply the filters by calling the 'example_callback' function we\n * \"hooked\" to 'example_filter' using the add_filter() function above.\n * - 'example_filter' is the filter hook $tag\n * - 'filter me' is the value being filtered\n * - $arg1 and $arg2 are the additional arguments passed to the callback.\n$value = apply_filters( 'example_filter', 'filter me', $arg1, $arg2 );
\n\n\t
\n\n\t
\n\t
\n\t\t

Return #Return

Source #Source

\n\t\t

\n\t\t\tFile: wp-includes/plugin.php\t\t

\n\n\t\t\t\t\t
\n\t\t\t\t
function apply_filters( $tag, $value ) {\n\tglobal $wp_filter, $wp_current_filter;\n\n\t$args = array();\n\n\t// Do 'all' actions first.\n\tif ( isset($wp_filter['all']) ) {\n\t\t$wp_current_filter[] = $tag;\n\t\t$args = func_get_args();\n\t\t_wp_call_all_hook($args);\n\t}\n\n\tif ( !isset($wp_filter[$tag]) ) {\n\t\tif ( isset($wp_filter['all']) )\n\t\t\tarray_pop($wp_current_filter);\n\t\treturn $value;\n\t}\n\n\tif ( !isset($wp_filter['all']) )\n\t\t$wp_current_filter[] = $tag;\n\n\tif ( empty($args) )\n\t\t$args = func_get_args();\n\n\t// don't pass the tag name to WP_Hook\n\tarray_shift( $args );\n\n\t$filtered = $wp_filter[ $tag ]->apply_filters( $value, $args );\n\n\tarray_pop( $wp_current_filter );\n\n\treturn $filtered;\n}\n
\n\t\t\t
\n\t\t\t

Uses
UsesDescription
\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\twp-includes/plugin.php:\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t_wp_call_all_hook()\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t

Call the ‘all’ hook, which will process the functions hooked into it.

    \n\t\t\t\t

    Echo after Filtering

    \n
    \r\necho apply_filters( $tag, $value );\r\n
    \n

    Get Filtered

    \n
    \r\n$myvar = apply_filters( $tag, $value );\r\n
    \n

    Additional Filter Arguments

    \n
    \r\n$myvar = apply_filters( $tag, $value, $param, $otherparam );\r\n
    \n

    For example:

    \n
    \r\n$myvar = apply_filters( 'example_filter', 'filter me', 'arg1', 'arg2 ');\r\n
    \n

    With the_title filter

    \n
    \r\n$my_custom_title = apply_filters('the_title', '  My Custom Title (tm)  ');\r\n$my_custom_title will now contain 'My Custom Title ', since the_title filter applies wptexturize() and trim(), among others.\r\n
    \n\t\t\t\t
    \n\n\t\t\t\t\t
    \n

    \n\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t
    \n\t\t\t\t

    One fundamental argument that is easy to miss is specifying the number of arguments. Most filters have only one argument and so people drop the argument from add_filter.

    \n

    The 3, below is very important.

    \n
    \r\nadd_filter( 'example_filter', 'example_callback', 10, 3 );\r\n
    \n

    Otherwise you get the following error, such as this StackOverflow question(http://stackoverflow.com/questions/24198086/missing-argument-2-for-the-function-in-wordpress):

    \n

    Missing argument 2 for example_callback()

    \n\t\t\t\t

    \n\t\t\t\t

    Uh huh.

    \n

    apply_filters ( string $tag, mixed $value );

    \n

    function apply_filters( $tag, $value )

    \n

    Parameters:
    \n$tag — (string) (Required) The name of the filter hook.
    \n$value — (mixed) (Required) The value on which the filters hooked to $tag are applied on.
    \n$var — (mixed) (Required) Additional variables passed to the functions hooked to $tag.

    \n

    Right. Tip: this does not make sense, in case you missed it.
